    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer17118620305204338608"><b>Poet Ocean Vuong's debut novel is a shattering portrait of a family, a first love, and the redemptive power of storytelling.</b><br/><br/><i>On Earth We're Briefly Gorgeous</i> is a letter from a son to a mother who cannot read. Written when the speaker, Little Dog, is in his late twenties, the letter unearths a family's history that began before he was born — a history whose epicenter is root</span>
  <span id="freeText17118620305204338608" style="display:none"><b>Poet Ocean Vuong's debut novel is a shattering portrait of a family, a first love, and the redemptive power of storytelling.</b><br /><br /><i>On Earth We're Briefly Gorgeous</i> is a letter from a son to a mother who cannot read. Written when the speaker, Little Dog, is in his late twenties, the letter unearths a family's history that began before he was born — a history whose epicenter is rooted in Vietnam — and serves as a doorway into parts of his life his mother has never known, all of it leading to an unforgettable revelation. At once a witness to the fraught yet undeniable love between a single mother and her son, it is also a brutally honest exploration of race, class, and masculinity. Asking questions central to our American moment, immersed as we are in addiction, violence, and trauma, but undergirded by compassion and tenderness, <i>On Earth We're Briefly Gorgeous</i> is as much about the power of telling one's own story as it is about the obliterating silence of not being heard.<br /><br />With stunning urgency and grace, Ocean Vuong writes of people caught between disparate worlds, and asks how we heal and rescue one another without forsaking who we are. The question of how to survive, and how to make of it a kind of joy, powers the most important debut novel of many years.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17118620305204338608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

No revelation seems to stand out more than any other. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I thought it was in the title. That we have this fleeting moment on earth and in that moment there is pain and suffering but also this joy, in small t<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I thought it was in the title. That we have this fleeting moment on earth and in that moment there is pain and suffering but also this joy, in small things, of being alive, of having love that is authentic. <br />From pg 231: <br />"All this time I told myself we were born from war-but I was wrong Ma. We were born from beauty.<br /> Let no one mistake us fro the fruit of violence-but that the violence, having passed through the fruit, failed to spoil it."<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2811555465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2811555465" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2811555465?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=modern-lit">modern-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2811555465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12201018469483938602"><blockquote>
  <i>“All freedom is relative—you know too well—and sometimes it’s no freedom at all, but simply the cage widening far away from you, the bars abstracted with distance but still there, as when they “free” wild animals into nature preserves only to contain them yet again by larger borders. But I took it anyway, that widening.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>4 1/2 stars. Stunning.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41880609.On_Earth_We_re_Briefly_Gorgeous' title='On Earth We're Briefly Gorgeous by Ocean Vuong' rel='nofollow noopener'>On Earth We're Briefly Gorgeous</a> is quite a book. It is not surprising that the author is a poet, as this reads almost like a poetry collection - prose p</span>
  <span id="freeText12201018469483938602" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“All freedom is relative—you know too well—and sometimes it’s no freedom at all, but simply the cage widening far away from you, the bars abstracted with distance but still there, as when they “free” wild animals into nature preserves only to contain them yet again by larger borders. But I took it anyway, that widening.”</i>
</blockquote><br />4 1/2 stars. Stunning.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41880609.On_Earth_We_re_Briefly_Gorgeous" title="On Earth We're Briefly Gorgeous by Ocean Vuong" rel="nofollow noopener">On Earth We're Briefly Gorgeous</a> is quite a book. It is not surprising that the author is a poet, as this reads almost like a poetry collection - prose poems, each capturing a moment, a memory, a feeling, or an idea so beautifully. It doesn't follow a regular narrative structure, but is instead a series of snippets or moments. The style won't be for everyone, but for those who love the raw punches of poetry, it is a fantastic book.<br /><br />I found it difficult to believe this was fiction. There is something about Little Dog's story, a certain <b>raw honesty and earnestness</b>, that seems to come from a place of truth. Maybe because much of it does. The author draws on recent and historical events, stories of well-known figures, artists and tragedies to weave his fictional story with every inch of our reality.<br /><br />The book is a letter from Little Dog to his illiterate mother. He talks frankly about race, gender, sexuality, masculinity, grief and language, without allowing the book to be overwhelmed by the heavy subject matter. The last one - language - is a major theme, and the author explores the importance of language on both a micro and macro level - the choice of individual words and phrases, and the power (or lack of) bestowed upon an individual by having access to language and literacy. <br /><br />For such a tiny novel, it is huge in its scope. From the Vietnam War to Barthes to Tiger Woods to 50 Cent to Little Dog's first romance with a white boy, it's somehow both a philosophical book about humanity and language, and a deeply personal bildungsroman. <br /><br />It is impossible to categorize, but it is undeniably both brief and gorgeous.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12201018469483938602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Roxane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1151637-roxane"><img alt="Roxane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442511711p2/1151637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2897735677?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roxane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roxane" href="/user/show/1151637-roxane">Roxane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2897735677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9981689470046960592">Ocean is a brilliant writer and I am a fan of his work. I even published him once in PANK! It has been thrilling to watch him soar. The prose in this novel is sublime. The way he writes is just… exquisite. He writes the body so well. He writes about the complicated relationship between a mother and son with real tenderness, with compelling honesty. He writes sex better than almost anyone out there. There are so many lines that gutted me or exhilarated me or stunned me. I wanted to sit with each </span>
  <span id="freeText9981689470046960592" style="display:none">Ocean is a brilliant writer and I am a fan of his work. I even published him once in PANK! It has been thrilling to watch him soar. The prose in this novel is sublime. The way he writes is just… exquisite. He writes the body so well. He writes about the complicated relationship between a mother and son with real tenderness, with compelling honesty. He writes sex better than almost anyone out there. There are so many lines that gutted me or exhilarated me or stunned me. I wanted to sit with each line and just feel it as deeply as I could. The intimacy of the novel as a letter between a son and mother was poignant. That said, I just didn’t fall in love with this book. The prose was, perhaps, too beautiful, too resonant, without enough story behind it. That is a personal preference, the desire for story. As I got deeper into the novel, I kept wanting a clearer sense of where the story was going, I wanted to feel like there was more substance to hold all that style. I do still recommend this novel because I've never read anything like it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9981689470046960592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2838119314" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2838119314" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2838119314?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=2019-releases">2019-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-lit">adult-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-mm">lgbtq-mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult-contemporary">adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2838119314" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4371899323914809655">✧ <a href='https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com/2019/06/25/review-on-earth-we-are-briefly-gorgeous-by-ocean-vuong/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <b>find this review & others on my blog</b>
</a> ✧<br/><br/>“<b>
  <em>Dear Ma</em>
</b>,” within the narrator’s head—or it might have been his heart—the name begins tolling, very much like a bell, “<b>
  <em>I am writing to reach you—even if each word I put down is one word further from where you are.</em>
</b>” And although he knows his mother is illiterate—her education capped at the age of 5 after a napalm raid destroyed her schoolhouse in Vietnam—and thus, all his hours and pain will be folded in paper and put away, the words kept tumbli</span>
  <span id="freeText4371899323914809655" style="display:none">✧ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com/2019/06/25/review-on-earth-we-are-briefly-gorgeous-by-ocean-vuong/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>find this review &amp; others on my blog</b>
</a> ✧<br /><br />“<b>
  <em>Dear Ma</em>
</b>,” within the narrator’s head—or it might have been his heart—the name begins tolling, very much like a bell, “<b>
  <em>I am writing to reach you—even if each word I put down is one word further from where you are.</em>
</b>” And although he knows his mother is illiterate—her education capped at the age of 5 after a napalm raid destroyed her schoolhouse in Vietnam—and thus, all his hours and pain will be folded in paper and put away, the words kept tumbling out, catching fire as they went.<br /><br /><em>He</em> is Little Dog—a nickname given to him by his grandmother because “<em>to love something is to name it after something so worthless it might be left untouched—and alive.</em>” And <em>he</em> is a wound in the fabric of the world, and onto this letter, he is bleeding.<br /><br />In his first novel, “<em>On Earth We’re Briefly Gorgeous</em>”, Vuong assumes the voice of Little Dog, who writes to his mother like being pushed from a great height, tumbling down, snatching at anything that would prevent him from falling. The reader could just imagine her there, hovering just at the edge of remembrance: stooped with decades of working in factories and nail salons, wilting her like an unwatered flower—those places “<em>where dreams become the calcified knowledge of what it means to be awake in American bones—with or without citizenship—aching, toxic, and underpaid</em>.” A mother the tighter he gripped, the more she melted away—like trying to hold on to the reflection of the moon. Tenderness, resentment, delight, anger. Little Dog’s voice carried all of it when he said her name. It carried every blow, a shock of bright pain against his skin, and the gentle tales that soothed his fighting soul, and the words struggled with the contradiction. Another figure in the periphery of his vision: a grandmother, trembling with age, whose mind sometimes breaks, all the terrors pouring out, once a teenage bride, escaping an arranged marriage, “<em>her body, her purple dress…[keeping] her alive</em>” as a prostitute for American GIs.<br /><br />Neither of them whole because no one is ever whole in the aftermath of brutal war and its bloody end.<br /><br />And in another corner of Little Dog’s mind, creeping farther over it with every page, is Trevor. They met on a summer job on a tobacco barn Trevor’s grandfather owned, and there, they shared the sensation that they were absorbing each other, melting together in an blistering crucible. “<em>Did you ever feel colored-in when a boy found you with his mouth?</em>” But Trevor’s sweet, perishing beauty is withering into earth with every swallow of the painkillers he’s addicted to, lashed to a flood of misery and self-loathing, and theirs was a love affair as brittle and breakable as a twig under ice.<br /><br /><strong>Vuong understands the eloquence of violence, and his words buzz with a red savagery, blooming, drawing as much blood from the story as possible.</strong> Whether it’s his nuanced yet viscerally potent exploration of sexuality, or his simmering, mordant probing of family, first love, immigration and fate, his writing is a pleasure to read.<br /><br />Vuong shows Little Dog’s feelings as water shows ripples, and one can only assume that he must have drawn on some wellspring of sorrow within himself—growing up in America, queer and the son of an immigrant. His narrator, Little Dog, writes as if he is embracing his memories a final time, pressing hard as if to set them into his skin. He writes with the kind of honesty that bypasses language and finds its way into your heart, uncut. His words are sometimes as soft as a shawl that wraps against the cold, but other times, they cut to the quick like the rasp of a whetstone down a blade. Oftentimes, though, the alphabet seems to transmute itself into incoherent pitchforks, wavering as if this were a fraying dream. The result is a book that can’t be described without borrowing some of the author’s own language: “<em>I’m not telling you a story so much as a shipwreck—the pieces floating, lit up, finally legible.</em>”<br /><br />“<em>On Earth We’re Briefly Gorgeous</em>” affected me like the gentle stroke of a callused palm, and I wanted to lean into it and let it stroke me forever. I couldn’t stop reading, as if the words were a rope and if I only kept it unbroken I would be held by it, unable to leave—and yet, at the same time, I often grasped for a feeling of escape, a moment to gasp for breath.<br /><br />With Little Dog’s confessional missive before me, my own childhood’s brutalities shone through as they never had before. So much of what I felt reading Little Dog’s words to his mother—delivered on the page as soon as they felt the brush of the dark, unreal places where pain in a thousand variations and memory mingle—cannot ever crystallize into something small enough for words. <br /><br />Little Dog writes, each word more desperate than the last, “<em>When does a war end? When can I say your name and have it mean only your name and not what you left behind?</em>” The answer is not as easy as paring rot from fruit. But in his bruised and aching letter, for the space of a few hundred pages, Little Dog stops winging doggedly onwards, dragging the uncertainty of the answer, and lets it all spill out of his body, onto the paper, in search for solace. “<em>I’m breaking us apart again so that I might carry us somewhere else</em>.”<br /><br />I do not doubt that readers of all sorts will find solace in Vuong’s words, or at the very least, something to connect with in this capaciously moving and ultimately hopeful novel.<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="4371899323914809655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2698340076" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2698340076" />
    <a title="Celeste Ng" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/80835-celeste-ng"><img alt="Celeste Ng" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442458318p2/80835.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2698340076?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste Ng" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste Ng" href="/user/show/80835-celeste-ng">Celeste Ng</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80835-celeste-ng?shelf=debut-novels">debut-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/80835-celeste-ng?shelf=asian-am-lit">asian-am-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2698340076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17446134569092132874">ON EARTH WE'RE BRIEFLY GORGEOUS will be described--rightly--as luminous, shattering, urgent, necessary. But the word I keep circling back to is raw: that's how powerful the emotions here are, and how you'll feel after reading it--scoured down to bone. With a poet's precision, Ocean Vuong examines whether putting words to one's experience can bridge wounds that span generations, and whether it's ever possible to be truly heard by those we love most.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2819767323?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer13029956586408890913">May 31 marks the 200th anniversary of Walt Whitman’s birth, and the best present we could possibly receive is Ocean Vuong’s debut novel, “On Earth We’re Briefly Gorgeous.” The connection between the Good Gray Poet and this young Vietnamese immigrant may seem tenuous, but with his radical approach to form and his daring mix of personal reflection, historical recollection and sexual exploration, Vuong is surely a literary descendant of the author of “Leaves of Grass.” Emerging from the most margin</span>
  <span id="freeText13029956586408890913" style="display:none">May 31 marks the 200th anniversary of Walt Whitman’s birth, and the best present we could possibly receive is Ocean Vuong’s debut novel, “On Earth We’re Briefly Gorgeous.” The connection between the Good Gray Poet and this young Vietnamese immigrant may seem tenuous, but with his radical approach to form and his daring mix of personal reflection, historical recollection and sexual exploration, Vuong is surely a literary descendant of the author of “Leaves of Grass.” Emerging from the most marginalized circumstances, he has produced a lyrical work of self-discovery that’s shockingly intimate and insistently universal.<br /><br />The fact that we can hear Vuong’s voice today in America stems from a function of tragedy and serendipity. As Vuong explains in his 2016 poetry collection, “Night Sky With Exit Wounds,” his grandfather was a U.S. soldier who found a farm girl in Vietnam. “Thus my mother exists,” he writes. “Thus I exist. Thus no bombs = no family = no me.”<br /><br />That willingness to solve the equation of his own existence, no matter what its components, is a. . . . <br /><br /><i>To read the rest of this review, go to The Washington Post:</i><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/entertainment/books/ocean-vuongs-on-earth-were-briefly-gorgeous-is-permanently-stunning/2019/05/28/b1f8a1ba-7ff7-11e9-95a9-e2c830afe24f_story.html">https://www.washingtonpost.com/entert...</a></span>

<div id="review_2911801412" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2911801412" />
    <a title="But_i_thought_" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67012059-but-i-thought"><img alt="But_i_thought_" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1492523508p2/67012059.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2911801412?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="But_i_thought_" class="user" itemprop="url" name="But_i_thought_" href="/user/show/67012059-but-i-thought">But_i_thought_</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67012059-but-i-thought?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67012059-but-i-thought?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2911801412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17486277454910201511">So you go to a high-end restaurant with an elaborate tasting menu. You are served dishes with fancy names that involve sublimated beetroot gel and deconstructed potato foam, and though the experience is unique and artisanal, you go home feeling... unsated. My experience with this novel in a nutshell.<br/><br/>At first glance, Vuong’s book has all the ingredients of a winning novel — lyrical writing, fascinating themes, a topical premise. Taking the form of a long, confessional letter from a young Vietname</span>
  <span id="freeText17486277454910201511" style="display:none">So you go to a high-end restaurant with an elaborate tasting menu. You are served dishes with fancy names that involve sublimated beetroot gel and deconstructed potato foam, and though the experience is unique and artisanal, you go home feeling... unsated. My experience with this novel in a nutshell.<br /><br />At first glance, Vuong’s book has all the ingredients of a winning novel — lyrical writing, fascinating themes, a topical premise. Taking the form of a long, confessional letter from a young Vietnamese immigrant to his illiterate mother, the novel explores race, otherness and queer identity. What’s not to love? Sadly, the book ultimately felt hollow and unsatisfying due to its performative quality. “On Earth” reads like the product of a writer modeling his work on the idea of the “serious literary novel”, having reverse-engineered a novel out of a checklist of common criteria. One can almost hear the author plotting in the background (“If I intersplice this historical chapter with scenes of animal torture, it will be so literary”). The result feels forced and highly manufactured, full of writing designed to distance and impress.<br /><br />Even the lyrical writing, which at first appears the novel’s strongest suit, turns out to be an emperor without clothes. The text is continually yearning, reaching, grasping — trying to extract profundity out of moments without actually saying much. A sampler:<br /><br /><i>“A page, turning, is a wing lifted with no twin, and therefore no flight. And yet we are moved.”</i><br /><br />Do I sound harsh? I hope not. If I could speak to Vuong directly, I would say this:<br /><br />You do not have to fold your story into a mould that you think will appeal to a ‘literary elite’. Drop the pretension. Shed the performance, and we may find — underneath all those layers — a unique and valuable testament.<br /><br />Mood: Affected<br />Rating: 5.5/10<br /><br />Also <a href="https://www.instagram.com/p/B0YD4KMgYoN/" rel="nofollow noopener">on Instagram</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17486277454910201511" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2599401399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2599401399" />
    <a title="Angela M" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4685500-angela-m"><img alt="Angela M" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512600770p2/4685500.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2599401399?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela M" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela M" href="/user/show/4685500-angela-m">Angela M</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42111754-on-earth-we-re-briefly-gorgeous">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4685500-angela-m?shelf=edelweiss-reviews">edelweiss-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2599401399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16770069785579737362">This is such a beautiful book title and it was the title that drew me to read the description and request a copy of it. Not only is the title beautiful, but much of the writing here is as well. It’s described as literary fiction, but a brief look at Ocean Vuong’s bio after I read this book made the biographical nature of the story striking. This letter from a young Vietnamese immigrant to his mother who doesn’t know how to read is raw, impactful, achingly sad, painful to read. It is filled with </span>
  <span id="freeText16770069785579737362" style="display:none">This is such a beautiful book title and it was the title that drew me to read the description and request a copy of it. Not only is the title beautiful, but much of the writing here is as well. It’s described as literary fiction, but a brief look at Ocean Vuong’s bio after I read this book made the biographical nature of the story striking. This letter from a young Vietnamese immigrant to his mother who doesn’t know how to read is raw, impactful, achingly sad, painful to read. It is filled with flashbacks to his childhood when he is bullied at school, physically abused by his mother, protected by his grandmother. It is filled with stories and memories of his mother and grandmother’s past fleeing Vietnam as their pasts become part of his story. <br /><br />It is about a love between a mother and son. It is a story of a young boy trying to find his place in this country. It’s an intimate portrait of his first relationship as he falls in love with another boy. (A warning to those who might be bothered by explicit sex scenes. You’ll find them here.) The vivid descriptions of the times he spent in the nail salon where his mother worked were eye opening. There’s drug addiction. There are also poignant moments reflecting his love of his mother and grandmother. The stream of consciousness felt a bit disjointed in last part feeling more like random thoughts , and it lacked the cohesiveness of the earlier part for me., thus 4 instead of 5 stars. This book is not for everyone, but it’s worth reading for the beautiful language and amazing portrait of the Vietnamese immigrant experience, for the intimate piece of his heart and soul that this writer shares .<br /><br />I received an advanced copy of this book from Penguin Press through Edelweiss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16770069785579737362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2734257837" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2734257837?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=own-physical">own-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2734257837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12424988683055565852">I am out here stanning the success of Ocean Vuong’s debut novel! As a fellow queer Vietnamese American, it feels so amazing to see someone with my same ethnic and queer identities breaking through in the literary world – and so sad that we have to fight so hard for our voices to be heard. This book took me on a scattershot, beautiful emotional journey. It felt less like reading a novel and more like reading tender, poignant passages about several connected moments: our narrator Little Dog accide</span>
  <span id="freeText12424988683055565852" style="display:none">I am out here stanning the success of Ocean Vuong’s debut novel! As a fellow queer Vietnamese American, it feels so amazing to see someone with my same ethnic and queer identities breaking through in the literary world – and so sad that we have to fight so hard for our voices to be heard. This book took me on a scattershot, beautiful emotional journey. It felt less like reading a novel and more like reading tender, poignant passages about several connected moments: our narrator Little Dog accidentally triggering his immigrant mother by pretending to be an explosion, Little Dog listening to his grandmother’s stories of war and survival as she descends into mental decay, Little Dog reflecting on his gayness and the violence experienced by gay people both in Vietnam and in the United States. At several points I had little clue what was happening chronologically and where we were exactly in Little Dog’s life, and I didn’t feel too bothered by that lack of structure because of the visceral beauty of Vuong’s writing, like the moments he wrote about Little Dog translating English for his mother and grandmother and the weight that comes with that, how he wrote about so many specific moments related to immigration and trauma and resilience. I love even this brief passage that gives a small glimpse into the complexity of family and immigrant life, with Little Dog writing to his mother:<br /><br /><i>I remember walking with you to the grocery store, my father’s wages in your hands. How, by then, he had beaten you only twice – which meant there was still hope it would be the last. I remember armfuls of Wonder Bread and jars of mayo, how you thought mayo was butter, how in Saigon, butter and white bread were only eaten inside mansions guarded by butlers and steel gates. I remember everyone smiling back at the apartment, mayonnaise sandwiches raised to crack lips. I remember thinking we lived in a sort of mansion.<br /><br />I remember thinking this was the American Dream as snow crackled against the window and night came, and we lay down to sleep, side by side, limbs tangled as the sirens wailed through the streets, our bellies full of bread and ‘butter.’”</i><br /><br />How could you not feel something with that level of quality detailed prose?<br /><br />I give this four stars instead of five mostly because I feel like the romance weighed this book down. I just didn’t really feel like Little Dog’s relationship with Trevor contributed much to the book? Like, I appreciate the exploration of queerness in the context of being Asian American and within the context of an immigrant family. I also liked how Vuong wrote gay sex in a way that felt realistic in its messiness instead of doing what a lot of people – especially heterosexual women who write gay sex – do by glossing over its complexities and portraying it as seamlessly hot. But I didn’t really get much from Trevor and Little Dog together aside Little Dog dating a white boy with toxic masculinity issues. I wish there had been more interrogation of the power dynamics involved with dating a white person or even being intimate in any way with a white person when you have a marginalized racial/ethnic identity. Or I wish there had been more space to see Little Dog reclaim his power apart from his relationship with Trevor. My sense is that if the space devoted to Trevor had been both streamlined and redirected toward giving more structure to Little Dog’s relationship with his mother and grandmother, <i>On Earth We’re Briefly Gorgeous</i> would’ve been even more phenomenal.<br /><br />A great read I would recommend to fans of poetry, poignant and emotional narratives, and my fellow queer and Vietnamese and/or Asian American readers. Just check out this lovely line and then check out the book if you’re so inclined:<br /><br /><i>Let no one mistake us for the fruit of violence – but that violence, having passed through the fruit, failed to spoil it.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12424988683055565852" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2883731128" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2883731128" />
    <a title="Neil" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33119635-neil"><img alt="Neil" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544045847p2/33119635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2883731128?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil" href="/user/show/33119635-neil">Neil</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33119635-neil?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2883731128" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12857522066279442403">Recently, when I have opened my Goodreads web page, it has seemed to be full of people giving a lot of stars to this book and singing its praises in glowing reviews.<br/><br/>I opened the book with high hopes.<br/><br/>On Earth We’re Briefly Gorgeous uses a fragmented narrative to tell, or perhaps explore is a better word, the life of Little Dog, a son born to Vietnamese immigrants into the USA. The reader gradually pieces together the story of Little Dog’s mother (Rose) and grandmother (Lan) along with Little Dog’</span>
  <span id="freeText12857522066279442403" style="display:none">Recently, when I have opened my Goodreads web page, it has seemed to be full of people giving a lot of stars to this book and singing its praises in glowing reviews.<br /><br />I opened the book with high hopes.<br /><br />On Earth We’re Briefly Gorgeous uses a fragmented narrative to tell, or perhaps explore is a better word, the life of Little Dog, a son born to Vietnamese immigrants into the USA. The reader gradually pieces together the story of Little Dog’s mother (Rose) and grandmother (Lan) along with Little Dog’s own experiences growing up, especially his teenage love affair with Trevor.<br /><br />Ocean Vuong is an award-winning poet and this is very evident in this, his first novel. Many of the narrative fragments read like poetry and it feels as though every word has been agonised over before being committed to paper.<br /><br />I should have loved this book. I have said time and time again that I look for atmosphere above plot in a book and Vuong’s fragmentary, poetic style certainly works through atmosphere and imagery rather than story-telling. It is the reader’s job to compile the story.<br /><br />But, somehow, I just could not engage with the book at all. I think it was partly the effort that has clearly gone into the writing. Each word has been polished to become so perfect that the overall effect seems to hide the content from the reader (well, from this reader) rather than draw them in. For me, reading this felt like trying to penetrate a shell that would not yield to reveal its contents. That shell is undoubtedly beautiful, but I feel I am only admiring the exterior, not the heart, which, for a book so personal and intense seems self-defeating. Part of the problem I had is that the book is framed as a letter from the narrator to his mother. But it is made clear early on that the mother is illiterate, so we know from the outset that this is just a framing device to allow the author to give voice to his emotions. We know he is writing into a void, and so, it seems does he. I also have to acknowledge (trigger warning coming) that there is a scene fairly early on in the book that features gruesome animal cruelty which really upset me and made me hesitant to pick the book up again for a while and then very nervous as I was reading in case something similar should happen again. That’s a personal reaction as I am not good at dealing with animal cruelty in a book, but this is about my experience of the book so it has to include my personal view.<br /><br />My thanks to Random House UK for making a copy of this novel available to me via NetGalley. I’m sorry I did not appreciate it more because I thought it was going to be a top read of 2019 for me and I ended up disappointed. I would give the book 3 stars but the animal cruelty really got under my skin and detrimentally affected my experience of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12857522066279442403" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3211239355" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3211239355" />
    <a title="Giorgia ~ Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97546350-giorgia-reads"><img alt="Giorgia ~ Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597878668p2/97546350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3211239355?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giorgia ~ Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giorgia ~ Reads" href="/user/show/97546350-giorgia-reads">Giorgia ~ Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97546350-giorgia-reads?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97546350-giorgia-reads?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97546350-giorgia-reads?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97546350-giorgia-reads?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3211239355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13982353750725922328"><b> 5 Stars </b> <br/><br/>This is one of those books that reminds me why I read. <br/><br/>Sure, I read for pleasure and to keep at bay anxieties and worries that otherwise occupy my mind (that’s what my romance/chick-lit stacks are for) but <b>my true love for the written word came from discovering the beauty of depth and emotion that’s hidden within the lyrical prose of select writers.</b><br/><br/><b>To say that the writing in this book is gorgeous would be an understatement.</b> There is one measure I use to determine if I find a particular</span>
  <span id="freeText13982353750725922328" style="display:none"><b> 5 Stars </b> <br /><br />This is one of those books that reminds me why I read. <br /><br />Sure, I read for pleasure and to keep at bay anxieties and worries that otherwise occupy my mind (that’s what my romance/chick-lit stacks are for) but <b>my true love for the written word came from discovering the beauty of depth and emotion that’s hidden within the lyrical prose of select writers.</b><br /><br /><b>To say that the writing in this book is gorgeous would be an understatement.</b> There is one measure I use to determine if I find a particular writer/book worth of high praise and that’s if it makes me jealous. And boy am I jealous of Vuong’s ability to write so rawly that it almost bruises you. <br /><br />Of the top of my head, I have a few favorites when it comes to formidable, evocative but also heartbreaking writing, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/148348.Yiyun_Li" title="Yiyun Li" rel="nofollow noopener">Yiyun Li</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3354.Haruki_Murakami" title="Haruki Murakami" rel="nofollow noopener">Haruki Murakami</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/176372.Madeline_Miller" title="Madeline Miller" rel="nofollow noopener">Madeline Miller</a> to name a few. Today I’ve just added Ocean Vuong to the list. <br /><br />I’ve forgotten how much <b>
  <i>I love to stare at a phrase and reread it in my head until it involuntarily imprints itself in my memory</i>
</b>. I tend to read a lot of <i>“feel good, easy to digest”</i> books with simple writing, for the obvious fact that I won’t dwell on them, I won’t torture myself with existential questions and most importantly I can file them away as soon as I’m done. There will be no extra burden on my mind, I won’t obsess for days questioning life, meaning, history, etc. <br /><br />But sometimes I want to invite that kind of reaction, I want to feel, I wanna be awed and lured in by gorgeous words that cut deep and then I wanna be healed of their bruising force, by extending my own understanding and contemplation to their meaning and purpose. <br /><b>I did all that with this book. And I loved every second of it.</b><br /><br />I realise this sounds more like a diary entry than a review but I feel like I don’t need to talk about plot, characters, or any of the usual suspects because this book inspires so much more than a clinical analysis. So pick it up and enjoy it, don’t give it that much thought. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13982353750725922328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3011205785" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3011205785" />
    <a title="Will Byrnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes"><img alt="Will Byrnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291462190p2/1526851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3011205785?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will Byrnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will Byrnes" href="/user/show/1526851-will-byrnes">Will Byrnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=books_of_the_year-2019">books_of_the_year-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=brain-candy">brain-candy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=gay-and-lesbian">gay-and-lesbian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1526851-will-byrnes?shelf=immigration">immigration</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3011205785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5714476901174866003"><blockquote>
  <b>I am thinking of beauty again, how some things are hunted because we have deemed them beautiful. If, relative to the history of our planet, an individual life is so short, a blink of an eye, as they say, then to be gorgeous, even from the day you’re born to the day you die, is to be gorgeous only briefly…sunset, like survival, exists only on the verge of its own disappearing. To be gorgeous, you must first be seen, but to be seen allows you to be hunted.<br/><br/>======================================<br/>“</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5714476901174866003" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>I am thinking of beauty again, how some things are hunted because we have deemed them beautiful. If, relative to the history of our planet, an individual life is so short, a blink of an eye, as they say, then to be gorgeous, even from the day you’re born to the day you die, is to be gorgeous only briefly…sunset, like survival, exists only on the verge of its own disappearing. To be gorgeous, you must first be seen, but to be seen allows you to be hunted.<br><br>======================================<br>“Everything good is somewhere else, baby. I’m telling you.” </b>
</blockquote>Take one beam of light. Direct it through a prism. It will separate into its component colors. Reading Ocean Vuong is a bit like this. He takes words, images, and concepts, beams them through his prismatic, gravitic artistry, and the result is a spreading rainbow, bending in several directions. It is a bit of a trip reading <i>On Earth We’re Briefly Gorgeous</i>. Go ahead, take the Vuong acid. This is a trip worth taking.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576059740i/28593952._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Ocean Vuong</b> - image from <i>The Guardian</i> - credit Adrian Pope<br><br><i>On Earth…</i> is not all straightforward story-telling, although there is plenty of that in here. It is a mix of elements. <br><br>The parts. The form. Little Dog is writing an extended letter to his mother, Rose, telling her of his experiences, a letter she will not, cannot ever read. He had tried teaching her to read English, but she gave up in short order, claiming that she had gotten that far being able to see, so did not really need it. Uncomfortable, too, with the dis-order of a child teaching a parent. The story of helping at the nail salon where she worked, where the workers inhale culture as well as toxic chemicals.<blockquote>
  <b>In the nail salon, <i>sorry</i> is a tool one used to pander until the word itself becomes currency. It no longer merely apologizes, but insists, reminds: <i>I'm here, right here, beneath you. </i> It is the lowering of oneself so that the client feels right, superior, and charitable. In the nail salon, one’s definition of <i>sorry</i> is deranged into a new work entirely, one that’s charged and reused as both power and defacement at once. Being sorry pays, being sorry even, or especially, when one has no fault, is worth every self-deprecating syllable the mouth allows. Because the mouth must eat.</b>
</blockquote>The History. Family. Little Dog tells of his grandmother, Lan, in Viet Nam, marrying a GI, bearing him a child, Little Dog’s mother. Being left behind when the USA fled. His history with his grandmother, their closeness, how she protected him as much as she could. When he was tasked with plucking the white hairs from her head, she would tell him stories.<blockquote>
  <b>As I plucked, the blank walls around us did not so much fill with fantastical landscapes as open to them, the plaster disintegrating to reveal the past behind it. Scenes from the war, mythologies of manlike monkeys, of ancient ghost catchers from the hills of Da Lat who were paid in jugs of rice wine, who traveled through villages with packs of wild dogs and spells written on palm leaves to dispel evil spirits.</b>
</blockquote> The story of his mother, growing up in Viet Nam, ostracized for being too white, her PTSD as an adult, and how that manifested as physical abuse of her son. <blockquote>
  <b>Sometimes you are erased before you are given the choice of stating who you are.</b>
</blockquote>The story of Little Dog’s contending with the dual challenges of being a yellow boy in a white place, (Hartford, Connecticut), in the poorer parts, and a gay one, to boot. Coming of age as a gay male teenager, first experiencing sex and a lasting relationship, until well, you’ll see. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576146137i/28598641._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="xxx" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Ocean Vuong aged two with his mother and aunt at Philippines refugee camp</b> - image from 2017 Guardian interview<br><br>The story of his relationship with his American grandfather, and a secret in that bond.<br><br>He writes about Tiger Woods, offering some history of how he came by his name, and wonders why Woods is only very rarely referred to as half-Asian.<br><br>There is much consideration of language. In an interview with PBS, Vuong talked about how in Vietnamese culture, farm workers would sing as they worked, merging the action of their bodies with the rhythms of the songs and poems. Other elements contribute to his perspective. Vuong talks about his struggles in school.<blockquote>
<b>Reading was particularly hard, and he suspects that dyslexia runs in his family, though he says now: “I think perhaps the disability helped me a bit, because I write very slowly and see words as objects. I’m always trying to look for words inside words. It’s so beautiful to me that the word laughter is inside slaughter.”</b> - from The Rumpus</blockquote>He writes of the body as a form of language. <blockquote>
  <b>I am writing you from inside a body that used to be yours. Which is to say, I am writing as a son. If we are lucky, the end of the sentence is where we might begin. If we are lucky, something is passed on, another alphabet written in the blood, sinew, and neuron…</b>
</blockquote>And <blockquote>
  <b>It’s in these moments, next to you, that I envy words for doing what we can never do—how they can tell all of themselves simply by standing still, simply by being. <br>Imagine I could lie down beside you and my whole body, every cell, radiates a clear, singular meaning, not so much a writer as a word pressed down beside you. </b>
</blockquote>The sadness of loss permeates. Little Dog has his own losses to grieve, his mother and grandmother far more. But there is recognition, also, that the trials of the past have allowed for some of the good things of the present. This is not a pity party. <br><br>Gruesomeness, having to do with macaques, is very far from gorgeous, but is fleeting, and can be seen as an image of the darkest sort of colonialism. There is also LOL humor in the occasional mismatch of cultures. <br><br>Vuong can start off a chapter writing about a table, for example, and turn that into a labyrinth, that winds, bends and turns, and somehow winds up back at the table. Very <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=usNsCeOV4GM" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> Somebody spoke and I went into a dream</a>.<br><br>This is one of the more quotable books you will read. A few:<blockquote>
<b>Freedom, I am told, is nothing but the distance between the hunter and the prey.</b><br>or<br><b> the past never a fixed and dormant landscape but one that is re-seen. Whether we want to or not, we are traveling in a spiral, we are creating something new from what is gone.</b><br>or<br><b> I want to insist that our being alive is beautiful enough to be worthy of replication. And so what? So what if all I ever made of my life was more of it?</b>
</blockquote>You get the idea. And plenty more where those came from.<br><br>While this is a small book in size, it is neither a slight, nor an easy read. You do not have to be a poet, or a fan of poetry to appreciate the wonderfulness of this book, but it wouldn’t hurt. The stories Ocean Vuong tells are clear and very accessible, but the linguistic gymnastics can leave you needing to uncross your eyes, more than once. But gymnastics are stimulating too, and might loosen up some latent cranial muscles. <i>We</i> may or may not be gorgeous briefly, or at all, but this book is a work of surpassing beauty, and will remain so forever. <br><br><br>Review posted – December 13, 2019<br><br>Publication date – June 4, 2019<br><br>=============================<b>EXTRA STUFF</b><br><br>Links to the author’s <a href="https://www.oceanvuong.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">personal</a>, <a href="https://oceanvuong.tumblr.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> and <a href="https://www.instagram.com/ocean_vuong/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> pages<br><br>Vuong is an award-winning poet. <i>On Earth We’re Briefly Gorgeous</i> is his first novel. <br><br><b>Interviews</b><br>-----The Paris Review – June 5, 2019 - <a href="https://www.theparisreview.org/blog/2019/06/05/survival-as-a-creative-force-an-interview-with-ocean-vuong/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Survival as a Creative Force: An Interview with Ocean Vuong</a> - by Spencer Quong<br>-----The Guardian – June 9, 2019 - <a href="https://www.theguardian.com/books/2019/jun/09/ocean-vuong-on-earth-we-are-briefly-gorgeous-interview" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Ocean Vuong: ‘As a child I would ask: What’s napalm?’</a>- by Emma Brockes<br>-----The Creative Independent – May 16, 2017 - <a href="https://thecreativeindependent.com/people/ocean-vuong-on-being-generous-in-your-work/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Ocean Vuong on being generous in your work</a><br>-----LA Review of Books – Article is from June 2019, but the interview was done in 2017 - <a href="https://lareviewofbooks.org/article/failing-better-a-conversation-with-ocean-vuong/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> Failing Better: A Conversation with Ocean Vuong</a> - by Viet Thanh Nguyen<br>-----The Guardian – October 3, 2017 - <a href="https://www.theguardian.com/books/2017/oct/03/ocean-vuong-forward-prize-vietnam-war-saigon-night-sky-with-exit-wounds" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">War baby: the amazing story of Ocean Vuong, former refugee and prize-winning poet</a> - by Claire Armistead<br><br><b>Items of Interest</b><br>-----Excerpt – The New Yorker published this piece from Vuong on May 13, 2017. It is essentially an excerpt from the book. <a href="https://www.newyorker.com/culture/personal-history/a-letter-to-my-mother-that-she-will-never-read" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">A Letter to My Mother That She Will Never Read</a><br>-----The Rumpus – a 2014 piece by Vuong - <a href="https://therumpus.net/2014/08/the-weight-of-our-living-on-hope-fire-escapes-and-visible-desperation/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Weight of Our Living: On Hope, Fire Escapes, and Visible Desperation</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5714476901174866003" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer17146731397795107727"><b>
  <i>'all this time i told myself we were born from war, but I was wrong. we were born from beauty. let no one mistake us for the fruit of violence - but that violence, having passed through the fruit, failed to spoil it.'</i>
</b><br/><br/>wow. i am stunned. in a debut novel where prose so elegantly meets verse, a work of beauty is created and the world is a better place because of it. <br/><br/>i randomly came across <u>
  <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cQl_qbWwCwU&list=LLWHWlL5V1gg8qCffWviOfSw' rel='nofollow noopener'>this</a>
</u> video (probably one of the most genuine interviews i have ever seen) and i immediately fell in lov</span>
  <span id="freeText17146731397795107727" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>'all this time i told myself we were born from war, but I was wrong. we were born from beauty. let no one mistake us for the fruit of violence - but that violence, having passed through the fruit, failed to spoil it.'</i>
</b><br /><br />wow. i am stunned. in a debut novel where prose so elegantly meets verse, a work of beauty is created and the world is a better place because of it. <br /><br />i randomly came across <u>
  <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cQl_qbWwCwU&amp;list=LLWHWlL5V1gg8qCffWviOfSw" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a>
</u> video (probably one of the most genuine interviews i have ever seen) and i immediately fell in love with the delicate, but intentional, way ocean vuong creates words. the emotive gentleness with which he speaks is exactly how he writes and is a tremendous asset to his first novel. <br /><br />i will say that i found myself drawn to the more straightforward sections of story, the parts that explore the main characters family history, trauma, and identity. but the introspective parts that are more freeform and challenge the traditional narrative of a novel are worthwhile as well, even if i wasnt as invested in them. <br /><br />the incredible thoughtfulness and grace that ocean vuong uses to explore themes of masculinity, language, love, coming of age, and family helped to tell a hauntingly personal story; one that is undeniably gorgeous. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_2624700692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2624700692" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32804270-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564311252p2/32804270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2624700692?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/32804270-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780525562030" href="/book/show/39866294-on-earth-we-re-briefly-gorgeous">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32804270-michael?shelf=recs">recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32804270-michael?shelf=2019">2019</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2624700692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18186261498504809237">Thoughtful and tender, <i>On Earth We're Briefly Gorgeous</i> meditates on the powers of storytelling. The autobiographical novel’s framed as a letter from a queer Vietnamese son, Little Dog, to his illiterate single mother, Rose. Across three expansive parts Little Dog reflects on his turbulent youth spent in Hartford, Connecticut, and hopes that the act of remembering family history through writing might heal longstanding wounds and bring parent and child closer. Using as guideposts the works of thin</span>
  <span id="freeText18186261498504809237" style="display:none">Thoughtful and tender, <i>On Earth We're Briefly Gorgeous</i> meditates on the powers of storytelling. The autobiographical novel’s framed as a letter from a queer Vietnamese son, Little Dog, to his illiterate single mother, Rose. Across three expansive parts Little Dog reflects on his turbulent youth spent in Hartford, Connecticut, and hopes that the act of remembering family history through writing might heal longstanding wounds and bring parent and child closer. Using as guideposts the works of thinkers as diverse as Elaine Scarry and Qiu Miaojin, the narrator roams among a wide array of shared memories, from his mother's harrowing acts of abuse to her infrequent but intense displays of affection. So, too, does Little Dog contemplate the nuances of his relationships with his grandmother, his absentee father, and his first love, and he reckons with how the legacy of the Vietnam War and the experience of immigration impacted his parents and grandparents. Sketching a moving portrait of a fraught bond, Vuong establishes himself as a promising novelist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18186261498504809237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3093604927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3093604927" />
    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3093604927?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3093604927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15018137026153009964">This is a literary feast, poetic, lyrical, heart wrenching, amazing story! My emotions are everywhere and I am so shaken, stunned, speechless and never thought this book could get affected me deeply. I think I should a few steps to get closer to the wall and hit my head to punish myself again and again when I routinely do for waiting too long to start a beautiful book!<br/><br/>This is a poignant, unique, heart capturing, meaningful letter of Vietnam immigrant to his mother who doesn’t know how to read wh</span>
  <span id="freeText15018137026153009964" style="display:none">This is a literary feast, poetic, lyrical, heart wrenching, amazing story! My emotions are everywhere and I am so shaken, stunned, speechless and never thought this book could get affected me deeply. I think I should a few steps to get closer to the wall and hit my head to punish myself again and again when I routinely do for waiting too long to start a beautiful book!<br /><br />This is a poignant, unique, heart capturing, meaningful letter of Vietnam immigrant to his mother who doesn’t know how to read which is including too many unspoken words between them. This is a story about a boy who tries to discover his true self in a foreign country, trying too hard to find a proper fitting, a real place for himself. It’s about his first love, drug addiction, his miscommunication with his own mother and grandmother, his suffers from bullies and his mother’s abuses. It also brings out the pasts of those two women and connects with the boy’s life story.<br /> <br />It’s not a hearts and flowers kind of soft, sweet reading or some heartwarming and emotional biography, this is so realistic, so harsh, including explicit and intense sex scenes and heavily depressing stuff so even though it is a lyrical, beautifully written and unputdownable journey, this book is not everyone’s cup of tea. If you want to start reading this you gotta prefer something stronger ( straight bourbon or at least dark roast-sugarless and creamless venti coffee)<br /><br />Some parts of the book were quiet challenging for me but at the end I got so much impressed by the raw and incredible talent of the author and how he creates magic by only touching the words. So I’m cutting one of my stars for the compelling parts and giving remarkable, heart wrenching, challenging four stars!<br /><br />It’s one of the different, adventurous, exhausting but also inventive reads of mine in this year.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15018137026153009964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review3093604927">
  <td colspan="2">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2910461067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17015718299793802627">With a title like this, an author whose name is Ocean and the remarkable reviews, I thought this would surely be a great one. Little Dog writes to his mother in such a raw emotional and passionate way. He reflects on his life -in his 20’s- the relationship with his mother who abused him at the same time suffering from her own mental<br/>Illness having survived the Vietnam war; his own journey through sexual exploration of his own orientation to finding himself; and the relationships he’s had with fam</span>
  <span id="freeText17015718299793802627" style="display:none">With a title like this, an author whose name is Ocean and the remarkable reviews, I thought this would surely be a great one. Little Dog writes to his mother in such a raw emotional and passionate way. He reflects on his life -in his 20’s- the relationship with his mother who abused him at the same time suffering from her own mental<br />Illness having survived the Vietnam war; his own journey through sexual exploration of his own orientation to finding himself; and the relationships he’s had with family.<br /><br />Poetic and explicit - this wasn’t a book I felt comfortable reading and won’t be for everyone.<br />It’s dark and quite sad with brief moments of joy confused with pain. Intense.<br /><br />Vuong can certainly write in a way I’ve never read before. Did I love it? No.<br />Will I remember it? Very likely. 4⭐️<br /></span>
